High Court Prosecutor Appeals Yi Fangshuo's Not Guilty Verdict 136

Yi Fangshuo, head of the Fangshuo Spirit Troupe, a Hangzhou native who performs comedic song and dance dramas at the rooftop playground of the Xinxin Company on Nanjing Road, is 44 years old. He was previously charged with raping his cousin. The French police arrested Yi Fangshuo and brought him to the Second Special Court. During the investigation, it was also found that Yi bought women to learn opera and monitored their actions, which constituted the crime of interfering with family freedom. After prosecution, regarding rape and disrupting public morals, the plaintiffs Ye Baozhu and Li Xiaozhen requested withdrawal of the case. As a result of the trial, Yi was found guilty of interference and sentenced to three years in prison. He was found not guilty of interfering with family freedom, and the charges of disrupting public morals were not accepted. He was ordered to be held in custody pending instructions. Yi was not satisfied and appealed to the Third Branch of the High Court. As a result, the verdict was changed, the criminal law clauses were amended, and the original sentence was maintained. Yi again appealed to the Supreme Court, which finally revoked the original verdict and sent the case back for retrial. The Third Branch of the Court opened a trial on September 17 of this year and concluded on the 21st of the same month, acquitting the defendant. During the appeal period, he was allowed to be released on bail pending summons. Yi was detained in the detention center for ten months. After being released on bail, he first went to Hangzhou to take care of family affairs and then went to Suzhou for sightseeing. He did not return to the Xinxin Company to perform again until the first day of this month. The details have been published in the newspapers. Now it is learned that the prosecutor of the Third Branch of the High Court has expressed dissatisfaction with the verdict of acquittal in Yi Fangshuo's retrial and has submitted a written statement of reasons to Chief Prosecutor Zhao Shibei, appealing to the Office of the Prosecutor General of the Supreme Court in Nanjing. It is not known how the Supreme Court will rule on this retrial appeal in the future.

Jin Jinfeng, 20 years old, wife of Weng Tianming, a farmer from Panjiashan Village in Sian Town, Zhejiang Province, was lured by Old Woman Dong from the same village on the 25th of last month to Shanghai to be sold. Shen, the squad leader of the Detective Squad of the Ximen Public Security Bureau, and Deputy Squad Leader Luo received a secret report and immediately ordered their subordinates to investigate on Jumen Road. Jin Jinfeng, the abducted woman, confessed that she was 20 years old, from Panjiashan in Sian. Old Woman Dong from the same village often said that Shanghai was a good place and persuaded her to come together. On August 25th, Old Woman Dong first took her to Taizhou and stayed for eight days, and then entrusted her to someone else to take her to Shanghai. She was not familiar with the road and let them take charge. She had been raped by Pan Jinyuan (aka Little Nanjing) for two nights. Her husband's name is Weng Tianming, 18 years old, and lives in Panjiashan, about two miles from Sian. After hearing the confessions, Squad Leader Shen dispatched detectives to arrest Pan Jinyuan and Four Eyes, who were related to the case, and strictly pursued Old Woman Dong, Shen Genfu, Zhu Fugen, and others who were at large. Since the case involved abduction and rape, the abductors Pan Jinyuan and Four Eyes, the female offender Zhang Xiaomao, and the victim Jin Jinfeng were all sent to the General Bureau for investigation.

Embezzling Relief Funds for Gambling; Attempted Suicide by Poisoning, Rescued; Qin Tinghou Prosecuted by Police 139

Bian Yichen, Qin Tinghou, and others from Ningbo jointly invested 2,000 yuan to open the Shenji Chemical Supplies Store at No. 11 Jinyu Lane, Edward Road. Bian served as the manager, and Qin was responsible for purchasing and sales. Last month, Qin sold 2,400 yuan of chemical supplies and did not hand over the relief funds to the relief office. Instead, he issued four checks from Tongyuan Bank, Municipal Bank, and other banks on this month's date to the relief office as a stopgap measure. From that day on, Qin did not go to the store to work. He went to the dog racing track to gamble every day. Within a few days, he was out of money. Because he could not make up for the loss, he had the idea of committing suicide. On the night of the 15th of the month, he went to Room 133 of the Xinya Hotel on North Sichuan Road and secretly took a large amount of opium to commit suicide. The tea boy discovered him and had him transported to Tongren Hospital for treatment. He Suizhen, the Chinese detective of the Laozao Police Station, learned about the matter and requested the First Special District Court to issue an arrest warrant, and then transferred Qinshan Tongren Hospital to the Municipal Council Hospital for treatment. He has now recovered. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. The police lawyer Wang Yaotang explained the previous situation and filed a public prosecution in accordance with Article 335, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law. Bian Yichen also hired lawyer Yuan Yang'an to attend the court with a civil suit. Qin Tinghou admitted that he had used a total of 2,200 yuan since August and was now trying to raise money to repay it. He also hired lawyer Fan Gang to defend him and requested bail. Because there was no shop to provide bail, he was ordered to be released on bail to Lu Pengling, a friend of the defendant. The court approved it and scheduled a retrial for one week later.

Gu Zhuxuan's Sentence Not Pronounced Yesterday: Because Several Points Still Need Further Investigation; Retrial Scheduled for the 22nd 140

Gu Zhuxuan, the owner of the Tianchan Stage from Yancheng, known as Boss Gu Si, 50 years old, was recently accused by Zhao Guangfu, Zhang Tingzi, and other criminals in the case of the assassination of Tang Jiapeng, the former manager of the Great World, on June 18, 1933, of instigating the murder of Tang. They met with Gu in Room 208 of the Asia Hotel on Edward Road beforehand, and Gu handed them a pistol and promised a reward of 10,000 yuan after the matter was accomplished. The French Police Department requested the Second Special Court to issue an arrest warrant. At noon on the 10th of last month, Western Detective Grell (transliteration) led Chinese detectives, together with detectives from the Public Concession Central Police Station, to No. 9 Yonghe Lane, North Xizang Road, and arrested Gu, bringing him back to the police station and transferring him to the Second Special Court for interrogation and detention. After investigation, the Police Department filed a public prosecution for the crime of instigating murder in accordance with Articles 29 and 271 of the Criminal Law. Gu hired three lawyers, Xue Dubi, Wu Kaisheng, and Lin Dawen, to defend him, denying the instigation and accusing Zhao and Zhang of extortion and false accusations. Court President Wang Gangxu, together with Assessors Xiong Huiping and Zhang Chaozuo, and Prosecutor Wang Ren, specially opened a joint collegiate bench on the 12th of this month to conduct an inquiry and interrogated prisoners Xue Zhenyi, Zhu Jincheng, Liu Yimin, Wu Shaoting, and others for testimony, declaring the end of the debate and setting a date for sentencing. During this period, Court President Wang convened a meeting of the assessors this Wednesday for the sake of caution to deliberate on various matters. The details have been published in the newspapers. Because Court President Wang, Xiong, and Zhang, who are hearing the case, felt after the meeting that there were still some unclear points in the case that needed to be further examined in detail in order to avoid injustice, yesterday was the originally scheduled date for sentencing. From 1:30 PM, the police continued to send Chinese and Western detectives and a reserve team to protect the court area, and maintained order in the court together with the bailiffs in the court. More than a hundred family members and friends of Gu who came to the court to listen sat quietly in the audience waiting for the verdict. At 2:30 PM, Court President Wang still came to the Criminal Court One with Assessors Xiong and Zhang and Clerk Zheng. Lawyer Fei Xizhen of the Police Department appeared in court, and lawyer Xue Dubi, the defense lawyer of the defendant, and lawyer Wang Shizong, the private prosecution agent of Tang Youmei, the victim's family member, also arrived on time to wait for instructions. The court ordered the bailiffs to bring the defendant Gu Zhuxuan into court. After briefly inquiring about his age, address, and occupation, he immediately informed the defendant that the Police Department's prosecution of your murder case was originally scheduled for today's verdict. Because there are still a few points in the case that need to be further investigated and examined, the sentencing will not be possible today. The closure of the debate is revoked, and the retrial is scheduled for 2:00 PM on Tuesday, the 22nd of this month. After the announcement, Gu Zhuxuan was taken back into custody by the bailiffs.

Huang Chongxiu, a woman from Sichuan who is nearly forty years old, met Zhu Pangu, who opened the Far East Film Company, through an introduction this spring, and then lent him a thousand yuan. At that time, Zhu wanted to create the Xiaoyao Dance Hall and raise shares from Huang. Huang invested 2,000 yuan and also transferred the 1,000 yuan previously lent to him as share capital. However, the Xiaoyao Dance Hall was not profitable for long and lost money. Therefore, Zhu sold the dance hall, and Huang believed that Zhu's behavior was fraudulent. Recently, she sued him in the First Special District Local Court. The trial had been opened once, and it was reported in the newspapers. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Feng Shide continued to open the court. The defendant came to the court with his defense lawyer. The plaintiff, Huang Suxiu, through her agent lawyer, stated the facts of the loan to the defendant after they met, and the process of recognizing shares and jointly opening the dance hall, requesting that the investigation be conducted in accordance with Articles 339 and 342 of the Criminal Law. The defendant, Zhu Pangu, confessed that the Xiaoyao Dance Hall was a partnership between him and the plaintiff, Jiang, Mr. Jin, and others. It started business on May 18, with a total share capital of 5,500 yuan. The plaintiff recognized 2,000 yuan of shares. In addition, the one thousand yuan was borrowed from the plaintiff by him personally. Unexpectedly, after operating until June 23, all the capital had been lost, leaving only five yuan and change. He immediately invited all the shareholders to discuss, and they were all unwilling to increase their investment, so they decided to close the business. Someone wanted to take over the business, so they transferred it, obtaining a transfer price of 4,000 yuan, which was used to repay all debts. Now, she suddenly dissents, accusing him of breach of trust and fraud, causing great damage to his reputation. Therefore, he also filed a counterclaim against her for false accusation, requesting that the case be brought to justice and punished. Judge Feng ruled that the evidence still needed to be investigated and ordered a retrial on the afternoon of the 25th of this month.

Details have been reported in this newspaper. From 2:00 AM to 6:00 PM the day before yesterday, the Chinese and foreign detectives in charge of the case, based on the confessions of the arrested Wu Kong the monk, Qiu Guobin, Wang Chenshi, etc., continued to arrest three more accomplices at the Sun Bridge, Singapore Road in Zhabei, and Foch Road in the Public Concession: Zhou Yaoshi (also known as Zhou Er Mazi), Liu Daosheng, and Ji Wenbin from Funing. They were taken into custody at the police station. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Third Criminal Court. Zhang Shizhu, a lawyer from the Public Works Department, stated that the three defendants were all involved in the post office robbery case and requested their detention and joint trial at a later date, presenting the arrested Wu Kong the monk, Qiu Guobin, and Wang Chenshi to identify them. According to the defendant Ji Wenbin's confession, he came to Shanghai from his hometown in May of this year (lunar calendar). Previously, at a certain place in Hongkou, a Mr. Liang, who is now at large, invited him to discuss the matter. Liu Daosheng was also present. He did not go to the robbery. Afterward, Mr. Liang received 300 yuan and returned to his hometown. Liu Daosheng confessed that he had a long-standing feud with Ji Wenbin due to a dispute over ear pulling and that he was being falsely accused. He claimed he knew nothing about the post office robbery and asked for leniency. Zhou Yaoshi confessed that he met Wu Kong the monk while smoking opium at Yanzi Nest. Later, Wu Kong visited his tiger stove teahouse on Sun Bridge twice. Although he knew about the post office robbery, he did not go to the robbery. Afterward, someone told him there was 150 yuan to be delivered by Liu Xiaosizi, but he never received it. His remaining statements were evasive. According to the arrested Wang Chenshi, in July of this year, Zhou Yaoshi came to her house and asked Liu Xiaosizi about the robbery. When questioned, Zhou denied it. Wu Kong the monk claimed to know Zhou and heard two days later that Liu Xiaosizi gave him 150 yuan, but whether he received it was unknown. Qiu Guobin also pointed out that Zhou participated in the discussion. Judge Xiao Xie Fen ordered them to be remanded in custody and retried jointly next Wednesday.

Dayuan Salt Manufacturing Company: Shareholder Lawsuit Concluded, Sentencing Scheduled for Next Friday 145

Wang Zhijie, a once-prominent official in the early Republic of China, recently raised funds to establish the Dayuan Salt Manufacturing Company in Yangzhou. His Shanghai residence is located at No. 18 Liang Yu Li, Weihaiwei Road, in the Public Concession of this city. In recent years, due to a lawsuit with shareholder Shen Kunhe, disputes have arisen repeatedly. Shen also filed a criminal self-accusation against Wang, alleging embezzlement of large sums of company funds and breach of trust. The First Special District Court has repeatedly held hearings and summoned Wang for questioning. Wang initially claimed illness and repeatedly failed to appear. He recently surrendered himself and confronted Shen, each holding to their own version of events. Shen then requested the retrieval of the company's account books, but Wang has not yet handed them over. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Ma Shide held another hearing, summoning both the plaintiff and the defendant for further investigation. After the facts of the various allegations made by Shen were heard, he ordered the start of the debate. First, the plaintiff's lawyer stated in his indictment that in January of the 20th year, the company was approved to increase the price of each dan of salt by 2 jiao, but the increase was not recorded in the accounts until August of that year. Furthermore, the litigation costs incurred by the company in the lawsuit amounted to as much as 5,500 yuan, and Mr. Ma was owed a large sum of money that was not recovered. He especially criticized the defendant, saying that salt prices were always determined by the government, and salt merchants never suffered losses. The company should have been profitable, but due to the defendant's private interests and corruption, it incurred losses. Furthermore, the defendant failed to register the company, so the voting rights still entailed partnership liability. He said he hoped that the defendant's mismanagement would be revealed in order to ensure that the judgment would be accepted by both parties and reiterated his request to retrieve the company's account books for detailed examination. Next, the defendant's lawyer defended against each of the allegations, refuting them one by one. Finally, he said that the plaintiff really wanted to obtain a position within the company, but when his plan failed, he initiated this lawsuit out of disappointment. Judge Feng then declared the debate concluded and scheduled the sentencing for next Friday afternoon. If he deemed it necessary to investigate the account books, he would order them to be retrieved for review.

Tianli Light Gas Factory: Concentrated and Dilute Nitric Acid Officially on the Market 153

The Tianli Light Gas Products Factory in Chenjiadu, this city, was founded by Wu Yun Chu of Tianchu Monosodium Glutamate Factory and others. It adopts the method of fixing atmospheric light gas, and the raw materials used are only air and water. This is an emerging industry during the European War. During the European War, the blockade of the coast of Chile cut off the source of Chilean nitrate, but the country was still able to support itself for several years, and gunpowder and explosives were not lacking, which was solely due to this method. Most of the various products made from this are necessary for the chemical industry and the military industry. There is currently no second factory of the same kind in the country. After the sale of various types of ammonia last month, business was booming. At the moment, various concentrations of nitric acid have also officially entered the market. Furthermore, because salt brain (i.e., ammonia chloride) is the main raw material for the telecommunications industry, the factory has cooperated with its sister factory, Tianyuan Electrochemical Factory, to manufacture it in large quantities. The Ministry of Transportation's tender for a large quantity of salt brain was also due to the factory's products being of high quality and low price, so it was decided that the factory would supply them entirely.

Must-Have for Postal Service Higher Examinations: Postal Regulations Published 157

The Higher Examination this year has added a type of Senior Postal Service Examination, with Postal Regulations listed as a subject in the second test, which is a subject that candidates must test in. However, postal regulations are relatively trivial, and rarely seen in newspapers, making it difficult to collect them. The Law Research Society, in order to meet the needs of candidates, has specially compiled the Postal Regulations into a book. The book is now published and covers all postal regulations, with a comprehensive and complete coverage. The content is divided into two categories: organizational regulations and business regulations. Organizational regulations include six types: Postal Regulations, Postal Law, Postal General Bureau, and Savings and Remittance Bureau Organizational Law. Business regulations include twenty types: Savings Law, Domestic Remittance Law, Simplified Insurance Law, Long-Distance Bus Transportation of Mail Rules, Subscription to Publications, Purchase of Books, Postal Telegrams, and Postal Aircraft and Passenger Return Rules. It is heard that the entire book is priced at six jiao, and the local sales points are the Writer's Painting Society on Simalu, the Life Bookstore, and the Law Bookstore at the intersection of Sanmalu and Yunnan Road.

New Legal Works Published 159

The New Civil Procedure Law has been in effect since July 1st of this year. There have not been many new legal books on this subject. It is now known that the Shanghai Law Bookstore on Sanmalu has published "Interpretation of the Civil Procedure Law of the Republic of China," written by Dai Jixian and revised by Guo Wei. In concise language, the book explains the meaning of each section, chapter, item, and article of the New Civil Procedure Law and integrates and cites relevant articles or other laws and regulations within the interpretation or provides examples. Because this book emphasizes both legal theory and facts, it allows readers to understand other articles or the application of laws and regulations by studying one article, saving search time. Therefore, it is praised by various jurists. Since its publication, it has sold very quickly.

Letters to the Editor 163

To the Editor,

Having read in your esteemed newspaper's "Letters" column on the 15th, the report about the conflict between the Wusong Defense Corps and the barber industry leading to a strike, claiming that the facts are inconsistent, and requesting correction, we were greatly surprised upon reading it. We hereby present several points for clarification: (1) The Defense Corps collectively referred to the thirty or so thugs on Taixing Road who were fighting each other. Why not state the cause of the incident and completely erase the facts? (2) Since Ban Wei Yang Zixiang is the plaintiff, he should be interrogated at the Wusong Police Station and not allowed to turn himself in. Moreover, Yang Zixiang is a squad leader of the Defense Corps and was injured. This is obvious to any discerning person. (3) Regarding the second arrest being deemed illegal, why was there no prior statement of the merchants' criminal activities? Furthermore, during the arrest, the entire armed force was mobilized, divided into squads, and searched each merchant's store, creating a menacing atmosphere as if facing a major enemy or capturing big gangsters. However, at that time, all the shops in the town were still open. Therefore, the public witnessed everything. Whether it was legal or illegal, let the public judge; there is no need for the merchants to waste their breath. Merchants have always known that your newspaper's principle is peace, and your columns are precious, so we did not fully disclose the entire process. What was reported on the 13th was merely a brief summary, and there was nothing inconsistent. Fearing confusion, we respectfully request a correction. We hope for your consideration. Sincerely, the Wusong Barber Industry Association. October 17th.

P.S. Our agency issued a news release on the 16th, which included a news item stating, "The Japanese Embassy will not relocate to Beijing for the time being." We have now received a letter from the Japanese Consulate stating, "The consulate did not issue this news item." Please grant a correction. Sincerely, The Editorial Department of the Zhongbao Newspaper, Guowen News Agency, October 18th.

Spring and Autumn

Snippets 164

— (Tie Wu)

Dreams are extremely sweet, and at the same time, extremely bitter; sometimes one dreams of sweetness never before encountered in life, but sometimes one also dreams of bitterness never before experienced in life.

You say someone is dreaming; others say you are dreaming. Without him saying it to you, and you saying it to him, "We are all dreamers."

Even iron men, when placed in nitric acid, will slowly corrode. Therefore, great heroes throughout history, when reduced to a state of sorrow, are always helpless.

When people are happy, it is best not to forget the bitterness. "Forgetting the pain once the scar is healed" and "Drinking today's wine today" are both extremely dangerous.

Poppy flowers are extremely beautiful, but also extremely poisonous. Using them as a metaphor for a beauty is indeed a fitting example.

A friend who, when you are annoyed, can refrain from revealing your not-so-public secrets is a good friend.

A Beggar with Ten Thousand Pounds 165

— Te

In a town called Cha in Portugal, a beggar often appeared. He was blind, and his face was well-known. According to him, he was penniless and suffering. Now, he has been accused of faking blindness to swindle money and has been taken to the authorities. It turns out that his eyes are bright, but he deliberately pretended to be blind, begging for sympathy. After a lifetime of hard work, he accumulated ten thousand English pounds. The reason he was discovered is also strange. There is a small town called Mour, a scenic spot on the coast of Portugal, which is very suitable as a summer resort, but because there are no hotels in the town, tourists are hesitant to visit. The local officials originally planned to build one, but they were troubled by insufficient funds, so they put the matter aside. The beggar was born in the town. One day, he suddenly visited the local official and offered to donate five thousand pounds to build the hotel, turning the desolate town of Mour into a prosperous tourist destination, and he was willing to personally supervise the construction. When the local official heard this, he couldn't help but laugh, thinking that the beggar was mentally ill, and revealed a sarcastic tone, which immediately angered this guest. He took out a checkbook from his pocket, indicating that he was indeed the owner of ten thousand pounds, and also proved that he was not blind but had sharp eyesight. The authorities were very grateful for his generous donation, but at the same time, they had to detain him because he had been pretending to be blind for thirty years, swindling people's money. After the news spread, the whole town was very surprised, but because this person was hardworking and thrifty, accumulating a lot of money, not for his own enjoyment, but sacrificing it for public services, so they all expressed sympathy for him, thinking that even if he was convicted, he might be elected mayor when he was released from prison!

The Happiness of the Dead 166

— Ye Yigu

In order to visit a friend at a rural primary school near Horbilan Road in Western Shanghai, I started from Nanshi and traveled a long distance to Zhaofeng Park. After arriving at Zhaofeng Park, I walked westward along Bailinan Road, laboriously reaching Horbilan Road. When I asked for the location of the primary school, I crossed Lincoln Road. The roadside was lined with trees, and the crops on both sides had ripened. As I walked and looked around, I arrived at a place with a colorful crepe signboard in front of the gate. Looking up, I saw the words "×××× Water and Land Dharma Assembly" written on it. Yellow cloth knots were adorned in front of the cement archway, and there were three doors leading inside. Driven by curiosity, I stopped and stood there. I asked a fruit stall next to me, and I learned that this was "Yong'an Cemetery." Because I had never visited this place before, I swayed my body and strolled in. I thought to myself: The happiness of the dead in these graves surpasses that of the refugees in the flood-stricken areas.

Hey! It would have been better not to go in. Once inside, I saw countless tombs in various shapes:饅頭-shaped, square, flat, and many others. There were marble tombs, and there were also white stone tombs. Stone tablets were erected in front of the tombs, engraved with portraits, elegies, or brief biographies, all luxurious and magnificent, truly worthy of being a city of tombs, a paradise of tombs. There were adults, and there were also children. I also saw many women crying bitterly in front of a tomb, their voices mournful, deeply touching my small heart.

I asked the gatekeeper, and I learned that the so-called Water and Land Dharma Assembly would last for seven days. The expenses were donated by wealthy people. Eighty monks were specially invited from a mountain near Subo.

On the way to my friend's school, I thought: The flood victims in the disaster areas are suffering from hunger and cold, waiting for rescue. Who knew that the dead in Shanghai have such immeasurable happiness? It is truly a contradictory thing that the living are not as good as the dead!

The Fragrant Shadow of the Imperial Incense 169

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Furthermore, the kang where the Empress Dowager was lying was not particularly special, except that the soft felt underneath was thicker than usual. In winter, three layers were used; in spring and autumn, two layers; and in summer, only one layer was used. This was probably because she was old and more afraid of the cold. The silk blanket covering the soft mattress was naturally extremely delicate and was changed every two or three days. Except for the summer, there was always a stove lit in her palace, burning more intensely in winter and more weakly in spring and autumn. At night, after she went to bed, regardless of the day, one of us eight female officials had to stay by her bedside. Outside in the corridor, regardless of sunny or rainy days, winter or summer, there was a group of eunuchs, standing motionless and silently, serving her.

Ah! These scenes, even as I think about them now, are as if I saw them just yesterday! What makes me doubt is why the Empress Dowager, who was so famous throughout the world, held such immense power, and controlled the life and death of hundreds of millions of people, was ultimately just a mortal human being. She also had to eat, wear clothes, and was just like ordinary people. She also had to wash herself—although the washing method was slightly different, wasn't the result the same, just removing the dirt from her body? All of this is enough to prove that she was still just a woman!

Furthermore, her senses were no different from ordinary people. She generally liked to rest and liked to bathe. Especially during bathing, when four palace maids used their skilled techniques to scrub her clean and tender skin, she clearly had considerable pleasure. (439)

Gathering Wild Chestnuts 170

— Wang Shapa

Tens of miles of mountains stretch out, covered in fluffy thatch. Several tall pine trees stand tall on the mountainside. A waterfall like a white chain pours directly from the stone crevices on the mountain peaks to a large pond at the foot of the mountain. In the crystal-clear blue water, a dozen black-backed fish swim around looking for food.

In the autumn season, the thatch is interspersed with many green burrs, which are wild chestnuts. Although the size of the wild chestnuts is several times smaller than those that are artificially cultivated, they taste particularly sweet and glutinous. The large ones are truly like Tianjin Liangxiang chestnuts. In our small village, we are surrounded by mountains, so there are quite a few wild chestnuts. The people who gather wild chestnuts are all teenage girls who carefully cut the chestnut burrs, being careful not to let the thorns prick their fingers. When they return home, they use a board to roll off the thorns and peel out the wild chestnuts, accumulating a large basket. Then, they put them in a pot to stir-fry them, bring them to the street to exchange for copper coins, about three copper coins for a small cup, which is great for children to pass the time. If you buy some raw ones and peel the meat to make a bowl of glutinous rice, it has a unique flavor.

If we carefully consider it, how much trouble do the village girls go through to exchange the wild chestnuts for copper coins? Recalling the various things in society, which one can be obtained easily without any effort? Therefore, as people, we should also work hard at our careers so that we can have a comfortable life later.

A Record of the Recent Situation of Ballad Singer Wei Yuqing 171

— (Pian Yue)

Ballad singers simply recite scripts passed down from their masters; occasionally adding a joke is considered improvisation. They are not necessarily required to have any talent before they can be popular. In today's world, there is Wei Yu, who possesses literary talent and can improvise and sing on the spot, naturally elegant and harmonious. In the ballad singing world, there is no match for him since Ma Rufei. His unsurpassed masterpieces include The Pearl Pagoda and Second Plum Blossom, which have captivated countless gentlemen and ladies in Jiangnan! Literary figures such as Qi Fanniu and those with elegant reputations such as Shen Anguan and Xue Xiaoqing are all his disciples. And Mr. Wei is getting old! At the beginning of this month, Mr. Wei was invited by the City God Temple to sing Second Plum Blossom, and the seats were filled every day; gifts were presented as souvenirs. A Mr. Zhou presented him with a couplet written by Zhang Zhenglü: "Don't refuse to sit down for another song, listen together to the master's Second Plum Blossom." The cursive script was bold and flowing. The lines flowed seamlessly, like a dialogue. Mr. Wei has poetry in his heart and knows how to appreciate it. Random Talk About Goldfish 172

— Wu Jiren

Many friends have asked me: Why do our goldfish, which are quite large and lively, die one after another after being kept in a very spacious glass tank for not long? The water is changed every day, and they are fed. Sometimes they eat it all, sometimes they just float on the surface of the water, constantly gasping. Changing the water helps a little, but in the end, not a single one is left.

I dare say that glass tanks are simply not suitable for raising fish; they can only be used for temporary keeping. Generally, a glass tank with a diameter of one foot, filled with eight-tenths of water (preferably with some old green water), can only hold three or four fish that are about an inch long. Give them some red worms to eat once a day. If it is not easy to get red worms at home, rice grains or porridge will also work, but they must be small and the greasy liquid must be washed away first. Also, do not give too much. Then expose them to sunlight for one or two hours. Change the water once a week, and they will not have any problems. If there is too much fish droppings at the bottom of the tank and it looks unsightly, there is no need to rush to change the water. Simply use a "suction pipe" to remove the dirt. At the latest, do not change the water for ten or eight days. As long as they do not float to the surface, it is okay. If the fish are large and the tank is small, they will not last even half a day. As for changing the water, both well water and tap water are acceptable, as long as they have been left on the ground for a week before use. This is called boiled water. Changing with boiled water has no stimulation on the fish's body. Therefore, it is best to use boiled water to change the water.

The above words are from actual experimentation and can be said to be the method of raising goldfish in Shanghai apartments. If you raise fish in this way, there should be no other problems.

These days, the autumn is clear and crisp, and many people are visiting Caohejing. Especially on Saturdays and Sundays, Guanshengyuan Farm is very lively. Therefore, the goldfish business is not bad. Those who go to buy want old fish that are three or four years old. So recently, more than a hundred fine old fish have been added from the Suxi area. There is also a type of pompon fish produced in the north. Two months ago, a manager from a Tianjin Guanshengyuan branch came to Shanghai, and I asked him to look for some large pompon fish after he returned. Fortunately, a quick letter came a few days ago, and he specially sent a fish farmer to bring thirty or so colorful pompon fish and large red pompon fish to Shanghai by train. Upon inspection, I was shocked. They were incomparably large. The pompoms on their heads were as big as two longans. They looked very good. They cannot be found in Shanghai. Soon, we will hold a "Fish Exhibition" of famous breeds from the north and south to invite celebrities from all walks of life in Shanghai to appreciate and evaluate them.

Finance Market 173

Tense Currency Exchange Market: Gold Price Rises Endlessly. Though Many Sell, There is More Demand Than Supply. The Price Repeatedly Broke Through 950 Yuan, Eventually Rising by 7 Yuan and 9 Jiao. 174

Yesterday, the gold market opened weakly. Unexpectedly, the surface was tense, and the currency market was depleted. Major players such as the Guangdong group vigorously sought US dollars. Although there were attempts to sell remittances, the demand exceeded the supply, and the price broke through the 50 yuan mark. In the early morning, overseas silver markets saw British silver contract while American silver remained flat. It was rumored that the market would stabilize after closing and that the US would continue to buy. Montreal forward silver prices slightly contracted by 1.5 to 1.7 li. Exchange rates continued to rise. London spot gold fell by 1.5 pence. Off-market pre-market trading opened higher at 42.3 yuan. Yongli and others even bid up to 34 yuan. Fuxing, Yongda, Dacheng, Hengchang, Yongda, Dahui, Xiang, and Wanxing sold, and the price fell to 39 yuan. Although Dacheng and Dingkang advanced to 40 yuan, Hengyu, Yongli, and Dada continued to sell, leading to further declines. The Central Bank's posted exchange rates were announced, with both British and American rates contracting. The Customs Gold Unit increased by 1.6 li. The standard gold price was posted at 940 yuan. Public sentiment was not affected. The morning opened with a low trading price. After opening, US dollars appeared in the Shanghai settlement, and the currency market hardened and fell. However, buyers took advantage of the low prices to become active, and short sellers also made up for their positions, which was able to maintain the market. Later, buying interest gradually increased, and the price broke through 40 yuan again. It was anticipated that HSBC's posted exchange rates would show British rates flat and American rates rising by 1.25. At this time, there was still a correction. As the mainland and other parties strongly sought US dollars, excitement arose. However, banks took advantage of the high prices to sell, leading to a decline. Unexpectedly, the Guangdong group worked hard to secure US dollars for December, selling remittances. However, because banks were not selling smoothly, demand in the market was strong. As a result, the currency exchange market became increasingly tense, and the gold market continued to rise. Major players purchased aggressively. Sassoon also bought forward shillings, finally breaking through the 50 yuan mark. Only then did many parties begin to offload their positions. It was predicted that Indian silver would only rise by a small anna, and the price quickly turned back down. At noon, public sentiment was still stable, hovering within the 50 yuan range. The later market was expected to rise as Shanghai supplemented US dollars, and the currency market remained strong, gradually rising and breaking through the 50 yuan mark. However, because of the sale of remittances by many parties, there were many trades in the middle. The initial report for Indian silver showed no change, and then a rise of one anna. After that, the price suddenly rose to a high of 955 yuan. However, banks took advantage of the high prices to supply silver, and Chinese merchants also stabilized their positions, and the market gradually turned peaceful. The second report from Indian silver showed a rise of one anna. Many parties made settlements, and selling interest became active, retreating into the 50 yuan range. Finally, the situation was flat and tired.

The morning opened at 938 yuan, a decrease of 2 yuan and 4 jiao compared to the previous close. Dada and Yongli Dacheng sold, dropping to 5 yuan and 8 jiao. Fuxing Yong Dingkang still advanced to 8 yuan. Dada, Fuxing, Yongchunyuan, Yongda, Dacheng, and Shenfeng sold, falling again to 6 yuan and 2 jiao. Hengyu, Dafa, Yongyuan, Yida, Dacheng, Fuxing, Yong Dingkang came in, breaking through 40 yuan, rising to 1 yuan and 5 jiao. It was predicted that HSBC's posted rates would show British rates flat and American rates rising by 1.25. Hengyu, Fuxing, Yonghengchang, Yongda, Dacheng, Richang, Wanxing and others sold down to 38 yuan. The mainland bought 6,875 US dollars for November. Yongli, Shenfeng, Huixiang, Dada, Dacheng, Yuanyitong, and Fufu all advanced, rising to 41.2 yuan. Hengyu, Fuyu, and Dingkang offered remittances at high prices, retreating to 0.8 jiao. Fuxing, Yonghengyu, Shenfeng, and Huixiang came in, rising again to 4 yuan and 8 jiao. Fuxing and Yongdafa Yong sold remittances, falling to 2 yuan. Publishing Industry

A Huge Crisis in the Current Cultural World 189

— Ping Zhi

The current cultural world in our country is facing a huge crisis. The arrival of this crisis is not due to the sluggishness of the publishing industry, nor is it due to the general depression of people's hearts. In a word, it is due to the new development of the cultural policies of imperialist countries.

Among all industries in our country, the publishing industry has, for many years, rarely been oppressed by imperialist forces. Like other industries, due to the oppression of foreign capital and the dumping of foreign goods, now nineteen out of ten are struggling to survive. National industries that rose during the opportunity of the European War have almost all fallen into bankruptcy. However, although the publishing industry is sluggish and the current situation is very bleak, it can be said to be detached from the oppression of imperialism. This is due to the existence of a completely different language barrier between them.

Therefore, the cultural policy of imperialist countries towards colonies initially focused on missionary work. The so-called church was also engaged in reprinting Christian classics, which had very little impact on our country's ideology. Subsequently, schools were established through missionary work, but they were still under the control of the church, with limited impact. Until the United States first returned the Boxer Indemnity, using it for education and cultural specialization, which proved very effective. Then countries such as Britain, France, Belgium, and Japan rose up to imitate it. Our country's cultural world became like feudal warlords who divided and ruled, and was divided into many factions due to differences in education and Boxer Indemnity basis. This process from missionary work to school establishment corresponds to the shift of capital imperialism from commodity exports to capital exports. In the stage of commodity exports, the purpose is to promote commodities. In the stage of capital exports, capital is used to invest in colonies, such as purchasing government bonds and securities, and establishing factories to seek profits. Therefore, in the stage of imperialist commodity exports, what is needed are commodity salesmen and so-called new people who use Western civilization products. In the stage of capital exports, it is necessary to further advance and need technically specialized talents. For example, when imperialists invest in building roads, they not only hope to obtain interest from railway operations, but also hope that railway materials and so on can be supplied by them, and that the management of the railway can be controlled by them. Here, people who have received their education are needed.

Until recently, the cultural world in our country was in such a situation. But we know that the policy of capital imperialism towards colonies does not stop at the export of capital. It also wants to further make the colony subordinate to its own country politically, economically, and culturally. This is the process of the vast China from a semi-colony to a divided colony. Unfortunately, our destiny now has to embark on the first step of this process!

Now, not to mention the political and economic situation, just in terms of the cultural world, we can clearly see that because of the oppression of imperialist forces, we can no longer speak freely, and even our textbooks and our history must be modified. But will the imperialists stop there? No! Like Soviet Russia, in order to promote its doctrine and communize China, it had compiled Chinese textbooks and other reading materials, and had also published many Chinese newspapers and magazines. Imperialists will inevitably come up with this set of tricks. Imperialist Chinese newspapers and Chinese magazines already exist. The textbooks edited by bookstores opened by imperialists themselves will certainly be published soon. At that time, I ask, can the capital strength of our country's publishing industry compete with them? In this way, our publishing industry, which has always been detached from the oppression of imperialism, will inevitably be hit by its dumping and fall into a desperate situation.

Or it may be said that even so, as long as our intellectuals do not cooperate and unanimously resist, what use will imperialists have even with their strong capital and power? But I dare to ask if this is possible? We must know that the general intellectuals in China today are proud to be close to foreigners, and the general psychology of society is that those who can interact with foreigners are high-class. The current situation is such that it is only that the imperialists do not use us. If there is any need, I am afraid that Chinese intellectuals will be eager to climb the dragon gate.

Do readers doubt my words? Then please look at the facts before you. Are those who divided the Boxer Indemnity not our country's so-called celebrities and scholars? And the so-called experts, are their research reports mostly using Western languages instead of being disdainful of using their own Chinese? Furthermore, the current so-called scholars, even though their writings are in Chinese, are they not sent to foreign printing houses or foreign publications and then distributed by foreign bookstores? Relying on the power of imperialism, they can occupy a high position in society, be respected by the general public, and also avoid the inspection of the government and freely publish their remarks criticizing the country, giving people the impression of being daring heroes. Who would not want to be such a traitor?

Since things have reached this point, this is the cultural elimination of China. If we do not make plans now, I am afraid that we will regret it too late!

A Readable Book 190

— Zeng Jianping

The Land Tax System in China's Medieval Period, written by Liu Daoyuan, printed by New Life Bookstore

In recent years, although China's publishing industry has paid a little attention to the problems of China's social system itself due to the debate on social history, the recent works that can make individual expositions and analyses on the historical facts of Chinese society are still a minority of minorities. Especially more specialized works on the issue of land tax are as rare as phoenix feathers. This phenomenon has become clearer to me in the past few months.

Liu Daoyuan's "The Land Tax System in China's Medieval Period", although not a specialized big book, although it only takes the land tax system of China's medieval period! That is, the period from the Yellow Turban Rebellion in the first year of Zhongping of Emperor Ling of the Eastern Han Dynasty to the An Lushan Rebellion in the fourteenth year of Tianbao of Emperor Xuanzong of the Tang Dynasty, as its research object; But this book of his, in its methodology and in the materials, is still a readable book.

Why is this?

First, it is because the method used by Mr. Liu Daoyuan in this book is completely different from the method used by Chen Dongsheng and others. He does not regard China's land system or tax system as an isolated phenomenon. On the contrary, he regards them as social phenomena restricted by the productive forces at that time, and studies them according to the class relations within this phenomenon. He does not simply lay out the facts of past history with a philological attitude, but wants to "show" the "relationship between the rulers and the ruled in the rent and taxation" at that time through his research.

Therefore, in terms of methodology, this book is readable.

Secondly, in the division of social classes, Mr. Liu's work also has unique insights. That is: he not only lists this medieval stage as a special stage, but also points out that this stage is a self-sufficient production of manors, which is characterized by "the standing opposition of state manors, large clan manors, and temple manors, and the state relies on military farming or equal land distribution to subordinate the serfs under it, occupying most of the land, and establishing a powerful royal power over the large clans and temples"; And he further pointed out that the characteristics of taxation in this century are completely different from the taxes before 1804 ("Two Han Dynasties and earlier") and after 755. Because the taxpayers before and after the Middle Ages were commercial capitalists and large landowners; While the Middle Ages were generally strong aristocratic giants and temple monks. The change of the land tax system is one aspect of the class opposition relationship, but Mr. Liu can solve the mystery of the social stage to which the Three Kingdoms to Tang belonged from one aspect." Such a point of view is much higher than the opinions of the so-called scholars who generally lay out historical facts.

Therefore, from this point of view, we also believe that his work is a readable book.

Third, Mr. Liu Daoyuan's book is also very appropriate and measured in the use of historical data. For example, when we compare the chapter in which he discusses "Two Forms of Land in the Three Kingdoms" with the works of Mr. Chen Dongsheng or Mr. Chen Boying, we can see how Chen Dongsheng and others use the historical data at that time, which is how flat, direct and superficial; And Liu's writing can analyze the relationship between the various forms of land ownership at that time from the special form of the land system at that time. All of these are features that Liu's writing does not have in other books. Due to this feature, several people believe that Mr. Liu Daoyuan's work is really a book that the general youth should be familiar with in the period when the problem of China's land system is becoming more and more serious.

However, according to Mr. Liu's own preface, this small book is still the fourth part of his Outline of Chinese Tax History. For the readability of his works, we hope that his other works will appear.

Bookstore Miscellany (Continued) 191

— Li Hengzhi

Fifth—Bookstores that Expanded from Running Magazines—They started a publication, found it was doing well, and had a wide readership, so they proceeded to run a bookstore. Examples include New Women to Wenming, New Life Monthly to New Life, Life Weekly to Life, and Dawn Monthly to Dawn. Recently, it is said that the Chinese Rural Economic Research Association and the Chinese Economic Intelligence Agency, due to the popularity of their publications Chinese Rural Areas and Economic Intelligence, expanded and established the Xinzhi Bookstore. Unfortunately, New Life Weekly folded. Mr. Zou is back and planning the New Life Bookstore. "Economic Common Sense" has sold widely due to the advertising effectiveness of the Shenbao newspaper, which led to the creation of the Economic Bookstore. These bookstores can also be classified into this category.

Sixth—Bookstores Expanded from Old Stores—With the rise in popularity of opening bookstores, many old bookstores have also expanded. New life has been injected into old shells. For example, Dadong publishes books on martial arts, law, etc., which is not bad. Suddenly, they collected a large number of manuscripts and established the very beautiful storefront we see today. The rubbings and calligraphy from Shenzhou Guoguang Society are very inexpensive. Suddenly, we see Reading Magazine and a large batch of new books such as Plekhanov. The Minzhi Bookstore is famous for selling Party doctrine books. Under the leadership of Mr. Yang Youjiong, they have also published many new books on international politics and law. The World Book Company is known for Red Rose and Kung Fu Knight-Errant stories. Who knew they would suddenly have many ABCs, and then a large number of university series, middle school series, and many other new books.

Seventh—No, there isn't any more. It's not that there isn't any more. If I add more, it would be repetitive. If you don't mind the tediousness, you can still divide it. At the very least, you can divide out a kind of "inexplicable bookstore." Not long ago, everyone blindly competed to open film companies, established inexplicably, and as a result, closed inexplicably. At that time, there were many such new bookstores. A wealthy old man listened to the instigation of others, took out tens of thousands to open a bookstore, but as a result, it closed down before long. Secondly, recently, important Party and state figures have opened bookstores, or even "semi-official" bookstores have appeared.

Also, yes, there are those "bookstores that take promoting culture as their responsibility" that have not been mentioned yet! But, which are they? Ahmen, we can only say: all bookstores are!

(3) The Capital of Bookstores

The capital of bookstores is not different from the capital of other industries in substance. However, in the collection of capital, there are differences due to the different nature of the investors. According to the ordinary fundraising methods, there are only three types: 1. Sole proprietorship, 2. Partnership, and 3. Company organization. Bookstores are similar. But you must know that the "opening a bookstore" business may be outside the "hundred industries." Not everyone knows how to do it, everyone can do it, and everyone is willing to do it. Therefore, publicly soliciting shares and organizing in the form of a company is not common, except for a few so-called large bookstores such as Commercial Press and Chung Hwa Book Company. If there are any, it seems that only Kaiming Bookstore publicly solicited shares in the newspaper a few years ago. Although other new bookstores also have company organizations, public share solicitations are rare. The reason is not that the bookstores are unwilling to solicit shares, but that even if they do solicit shares, no one will respond.

To know the source of capital for a new bookstore, one must first know how much capital is needed. If you don't mind being too broad, then we can say that as little as tens of dollars to as much as millions are the same. How do you say that? Don't you see that there are many who only print a thin few dozen pages of "books" and establish a bookstore name? Isn't that enough with just tens of dollars? As for millions? That's a bit of an exaggeration, but in reality, the need for capital for a new bookstore is indeed unlimited.

The best strategy for a new bookstore to use capital is to use all capital, except for a part of the necessary expenses, entirely on publishing new books. The development of the bookstore's business is determined by the amount of books sold. To sell more books, there must be more types. In this way, the bookstore's need for capital is endless. Because, for example, the cost of publishing a book is two hundred yuan. Once the book is published, the two hundred yuan must be paid in full (it is a different matter if the bookstore intends to make the printer and author "eat bad debts"), but the book cannot be sold out immediately. Even if it is sold out, it is not certain that all the money can be recovered. Therefore, the more new books published, the more "dead capital" is invested, the more inventory, the more bad debts, everything is "more," and the less working capital. Therefore, except for a few large bookstores that have reached their peak (?), emerging bookstores, especially those in the process of development, are constantly seeking new capital. Today, none of the bookstores on Fourth Malu Road in Shanghai do not feel a lack of working capital. This cannot be entirely blamed on the sluggishness of the new book industry. A part is still due to the "capital structure function" of the bookstore.

Therefore, the source of capital for each bookstore and the methods of obtaining it have to come from the following channels:

First, sole proprietorship. There are several types of sole proprietorship. Some are bookstore owners who operate the bookstore themselves and invest their own money. Most of these bookstores are shopkeeper bookstores, and their scale is not large. There are also non-operators who invest. In the past few years, there were quite a few military and political figures and advanced Party figures who, after listening to the encirclement and instigation of general literati, took out tens of thousands or hundreds of thousands to open a bookstore. Many of these bookstores have closed down today, but there are still one or two that, when they run out of money, the investor writes a check, and they continue with one check after another. In the past, some bookstores had no accounts in the business department at all. In one case, when the manager died, the outstanding customer accounts could not be found. Those who didn't know thought it was a joke. If they knew the inside story of how these bookstores raised funds, it would naturally not be surprising.

Second, partnership. This kind of partnership is more common in bookstores opened by literati themselves. A few writing friends gather together, everyone takes out some money, and the bookstore is established. But they don't know that new bookstores need new capital to nourish them from time to time. Literati simply don't have that much money, so they can't continue, and many such bookstores die halfway.

Various interesting methods of raising capital also often occur in this type of bookstore. For example, embezzling authors' royalties as new shares is one of them. Because bookstores opened by literati often have some understanding of books they publish, if someone publishes a book with them, they will say to you: "Half of your royalties will be used as shares to join our bookstore!" In this way, it is nominally increasing new capital. Secondly, to acquaintances, "Old friend, please join us for a share too." After the money is taken, the rent is paid first, or even the salary for the current month of the person who pulled the shares is paid first, until they close the door and everything is auspicious. There are also many cases where the investor has not yet seen the stock.

Third, company organization, but very few of the new bookstores in Shanghai are truly handled in accordance with the Company Law. In addition to one or two large bookstores, many new bookstores, although said to be joint-stock companies, in fact not only do not have official dividends, but also the annual business reports are not seen.

There is also a way to absorb capital, and it is not a very good way, that is, the bookstore absorbing deposits. Among them, the best is the World Book Company. In addition, Kaiming, Children's, etc., also have colleague deposits. The annual interest rate for bank deposits is only seven percent, while the interest rate for bookstore deposits is between eight and ten percent. From the bookstore's point of view, this is better than overdrafting from the bank at nine percent, but in the general decline of the book industry, it is difficult to have a net profit of one percent in business settlement. Therefore, the so-called deposits are actually drinking poison to quench thirst. (To be continued)

Modern Medicine Publication

First Aid Common Sense, Part Four 192

— Editor

(4) Poisoning (Fungi)

Fragrant mushrooms and tree ears are one of our daily edible essentials. Some of them contain toxins, so eating them can cause poisoning. Also, there are those that are not poisonous mushrooms, but are poisonous because the mushrooms have rotted. One must be able to distinguish them.

Those poisoned by mushrooms immediately develop acute symptoms in the gastrointestinal tract. Or frequent vomiting and diarrhea, or abdominal pain, or even strange thirst in the mouth, general fatigue, sweating, thin pulse, mania, drowsiness, and eventually death.

Before the doctor arrives, the following effective measures should be taken. First, induce vomiting. (For vomiting methods, see previous issues). The vomited mushroom pieces should be kept for the doctor to check whether it is true mushroom poisoning. If there is a state of collapse, stimulants should be administered immediately and artificial respiration should be applied to seek a turning point.

Shenbao Radio Weekly

Using a Positive Grid, Negative Plate Triode as a Detector Tube 204

— Chong Ling

Usually, with a triode vacuum tube, whether used for oscillation, amplification, or detection, the plate voltage used must be positive, and the grid voltage must be negative. Everyone knows this is a triode with a negative grid and positive plate. The input circuit is the grid circuit, and the output circuit is the plate circuit, with the grid electrode presiding over the control function. To reverse this, using the plate electrode as the control electrode, inputting high-frequency voltage to the plate electrode, and outputting from the grid electrode, has not been seen in practical applications.

The Positive Grid Tube has the same basic structure as an ordinary triode. The difference lies in the exchange of roles between the plate and grid. The plate takes on all the work of the grid in an ordinary triode, and the grid takes on all the work of the plate in an ordinary triode. Therefore, a positive grid, negative plate triode can also be called an Inverted Vacuum Tube. Its main points are three: (1) The grid has a positive voltage, so it can be renamed the positive grid. Because it is closer to the filament, the grid current is quite large; (2) The plate is connected to a negative voltage, so the plate current is small or non-existent. Because it has the main control function, it is renamed the control electrode (Brakeelectrode, to indicate the difference; (3) Since the plate and grid have exchanged functions, the input is handled by the plate circuit, and the output is handled by the grid circuit.

The uses of positive grid, negative plate triodes include the invention of the Barkhausen Oscillator in oscillation, to generate ultra-short waves from ten centimeters to several meters; in amplification, it can be used as a device to reduce voltage, because the input control electrode is farther from the filament than the output positive grid, its function is exactly the opposite of an ordinary triode, actually reducing rather than amplifying; for detection, it can not only be used to receive ultra-short waves, but if handled properly, it can also receive ordinary broadcast bands, and its sensitivity is not weak.

Figure 1 shows the wiring of a positive grid, negative plate triode. Electrons generated by the filament F are attracted by the positive grid G. Some flow into the grid circuit, and some pass through the grid gap to the vicinity of the control electrode B. If the voltage of the control electrode is positive at this time, this part of the electrons will be absorbed by the control electrode; if the voltage of the control electrode is negative at this time, then this part of the electrons will be rejected by the control electrode and fold back to the grid. If the grid positive voltage is raised to saturation, the total current emitted by the filament, is, has reached saturation and does not change. Then the sum of the plate current, ib, and the grid current, ig, must remain unchanged, because the total current emitted by the filament is the sum of the plate current and the grid current. Therefore,

ib + ig = is = constant

If shown in a diagram, the ig-eb characteristic curve must be a reflection of the ib-eb characteristic curve, as shown in Figure 2, as shown in Figure 2; in other words, the increase in plate current must be equal to the decrease in grid current. If the grid current increases, the plate current must decrease accordingly. If the principle of plate detection of an ordinary triode is applied here, the negative voltage Eb of the control electrode can be matched to the appropriate operating point, then the high-frequency voltage eq input to the control electrode, through rectification, causes the plate current ib to increase according to the input eb waveform, and the grid current ig also decreases along with the plate current waveform, so the detection function is transferred to the output grid circuit.

(1) Ultra-short Wave Detection Applying the above principle, a detection circuit can be obtained as shown in Figure 3 to receive ultra-short waves. The ultra-short wave high-frequency voltage is induced by the antenna to the matching tuning circuit E to reach the control electrode B, and the negative voltage Eb is configured to obtain the corresponding operating point on the control curve ib-eb. Thus, by rectification, the amplitude-modulated signal is delivered to the grid circuit. The change in grid current is made into a voltage change through the action of the load resistor Eg for output. In order to avoid excessive DC voltage drop of Zg consumed in Zg, eb is not a circumferential resistor, but a total impedance (Impedance). Since the current-voltage drop of the total impedance is very small, the Eg used only needs to exceed the saturation value to reduce the grid voltage reduced by the amplitude-modulated current is sufficient.

(2) Broadcast Band Detection Figure 3 can only be applied when the total impedance of the matching tuning circuit E is very small; if the total impedance of E is very large, because ib flows through the total impedance of E, this tube is bound to be insensitive to eb. The E circuit receiving ultra-short waves has a very small total impedance, so it can be as sensitive as an ordinary triode. However, for the wavelength of the broadcast band, the total impedance of the E circuit is sufficient to make Figure 3 inapplicable. To detect the broadcast band, Figure 3 can be improved as shown in Figure 4, and the operating point of ib-eb is configured at P, while the operating point of ig-eb should be q. c is a 100 M.M.F. capacitor connected between the plate and grid to allow a part of the plate current ib to pass through c, to reduce the load of the E circuit. In addition, a high-frequency choke D is inserted in the grid circuit to block the path of high-frequency current flow, while C's impedance to low frequencies is sufficient to prevent the rectification of the grid circuit from flowing into the plate circuit, so the rectification only flows through the grid load Zg. According to the results obtained from the test, the sensitivity of such a device is increased by 45 times compared to Figure 3, and it is not weaker than the detection of an ordinary triode.

Simple Superheterodyne Three-Tube Radio 207

— Cao Runsheng

The superheterodyne radio is the best circuit in radios because it has superb selectivity and sensitivity. Its special features are especially evident in Shanghai, where there are many radio stations. The principle of superheterodyne is simple: the incoming radio signal passes through a detector to become a low-frequency current, while the high-frequency current emitted by the local oscillator in the radio mixes with it to become an intermediate frequency between high and low frequencies. Then this intermediate frequency is input to another detector (i.e. the second detector) through an intermediate frequency transformer to become a low-frequency current audible to the human ear. The more difficult thing to manufacture in a superheterodyne radio is the intermediate frequency transformer. This device must be able to allow one type of frequency current to pass through, and other frequencies must absolutely not pass through. At the same time, the mixed frequency of the incoming radio signal and the local oscillator is always the same as the intermediate frequency transformer, otherwise it will fail. The reason why a superheterodyne radio has superb selectivity is also

Very few homemade radios use superheterodyne circuits. Most manufacturers think that superheterodyne is extremely difficult to manufacture and dare not try. However, many people are only interested in entertainment, so they disdain to learn more advanced circuits. In fact, superheterodyne circuits are not difficult to make. If it is difficult, then it is the responsibility that we amateur researchers should bear! Here, the author will introduce to you the simplest superheterodyne radio, which has several characteristics: (To be continued)

Of all the swimming events yesterday, the most tense was the women's 100-meter final. Eight people, including Yang Xiuqiong, participated. The original preliminaries were briskly changed to finals because there were not many participants. The number of swimming spectators yesterday was no less than the day before. Some even came from Nanjing and Hangzhou. As soon as the announcement was made for the women's 100-meter final call, all heads turned, and the crowd was roaring. When the Gun Sounds, a Group of Fish Compete

Yang Xiuqiong was in the front line, with Liu Guizhen to her left. Liu had defeated Xiuqiong in the 50-meter race, and had the ambition to defeat Yang again in the 100-meter race. Yang, on the other hand, prayed to avenge her previous shame in the 100-meter race. As soon as the gun fired, fish leaped into the water. The leader was Chen Huanqiong. Chen's body was short and her speed was excellent. She led the way all the way. At the 50-meter mark, Chen Huanqiong was three meters ahead of Yang Xiuqiong, while Liu Guizhen and Yang Xiuqiong were neck and neck.

Guizhen and Xiuqiong Compete Fiercely

At the 70-meter mark, Chen Huanqiong was still in the lead. Unfortunately, Chen Huanqiong was young and her strength was insufficient, causing her to be chased by Liu Guizhen and Yang Xiuqiong in the last 30 meters. At this moment, the competition between Xiuqiong and Guizhen was the most intense, and the applause from the whole stadium was endless. Guizhen once surpassed Yang, but in the last nine meters, Xiuqiong won with her speed.

The Last Five Meters Determine the Outcome

Yang Xiuqiong's participation in yesterday's 100-meter freestyle final was a dangerous birth, but she finally won the victory in the last five meters, which can be said to be a stroke of luck. Malaya Fought Hard but Lost to Hong Kong – Dominated with 2-1 Lead in the First Half – Intense Firepower – Li Huitang Led the Counterattack and Hong Kong Won the Final Victory 222

At 1 PM yesterday, the Hong Kong vs. Malaya football match kicked off amidst the sound of the silver whistle. The atmosphere of the entire stadium suddenly became tense. Malaya attacked first, and the Hong Kong army actively responded. They exchanged blows. After ten minutes, Hong Kong won a corner kick, which was taken by Cao Guicheng. The ball landed in the best position in front of the goal. After a fierce struggle between the two sides, Huang Meishun got the ball and took a long shot. The ball entered the net from the left corner. Amid cheers, the first goal was scored.

Malaya Attacked and Tied the Score

Having suffered this blow, Malaya tried its best to counterattack. After four minutes, it got a free kick opportunity. The right inside forward dribbled the ball and passed it to the right winger, Yin Jinzhen, who broke through the defense line and used his light feet to shoot the ball into the net. Bao Gang's eyes were fixed and his mouth was agape. The whole army was shocked and lost its color, and the score was tied at 1-1. Afterwards, the ball mostly revolved in front of the Malay team. Because of its solid defense and responsible goalkeeper, there was no loss of ground. The ball king Li Huitang was also under severe surveillance and could not find a way.

The Steel Gate Saved a Sneak Attack

At 31 minutes, the five Malayan forwards penetrated deep into the Hong Kong team's hinterland, charging left and right, and were extremely active. Center forward Xie Qingfu passed the ball to left forward Du Yachi, who dribbled past the difficult hurdle of Yu Qingyuan. The Hong Kong army was unable to save in time. Seeing the situation was extremely critical, Bao Gang left his old nest lightly and rushed forward to grab the ball. Unexpectedly, he did not grab the ball, and Malaya's left inside forward Guan Xinde got the ball and stole the Yinping Pass. The flying general descended from the sky, and there was an empty city. There was no one to resist. He kicked the ball, and it stepped slowly into the goal. Bao Jiaqian was unable to turn around in time and stomped his feet repeatedly. The score was 2-1, and Malaya took the lead. Afterwards, there was a long melee. The Hong Kong team's military strength gradually became scattered. Because the inner defense was weak, it was often attacked. The Malay army's left and right forwards fought swiftly, but their shots lacked power. The first half ended with a score of 2-1. The general audience thought that the Hong Kong army was discouraged, and some suspected that the ball king would not be able to do anything in the end.

Li and Chen Passed the Ball and the Ball King Scored

After the break, the ball situation of the Malaya team became even stronger. Although the Hong Kong army attacked several times, creating opportunities to attack, either the ball went out of bounds or over the net, and there was no achievement in the end. The military spirit was dispersed. Therefore, the Malaya team became more brave. In the end, the Xin goalkeeper relied on his experience and means to defend effectively, punching and kicking, and saved many dangerous balls. The offensive slackened slightly. At the 15th minute, the ball king got the ball and passed it diagonally to Zheng Jiliang. The Malay army rushed to Zheng to snatch the ball, but Zheng passed it to the ball king again. Li Huitang was surrounded by three enemies, but the ball was like a magnet, and it never left his feet. He dribbled to a place more than ten feet in front of the goal. Just as he raised his feet, the ball had already entered the net, clearly and beautifully. Some of the audience shouted "Long live Li Huitang." The Hong Kong army was greatly boosted, as if it had taken a shot of morphine. The turning point of victory was completely in this ball.

Malaya Fought Hard but Lost by One Goal

After being lifted by the ball king, the Hong Kong army's morale suddenly increased. The war record had become 2-1. The two sides engaged in hand-to-hand combat, reaching the point of melee. The performance was full of excitement and extremely tense. The audience held their breath and watched attentively. When there was danger, there were sounds of "Ah yo," which was indeed a vivid war. Both sides were careful. There was no record for five minutes. At the 20th minute, the Hong Kong right inside forward passed the ball to Li, who passed it to Liang again. Liang sprinted and broke through the defense line. The ball was like a bullet and was shot into the net from the left corner, creating a record of 3-1. Hong Kong won. Therefore, the Hong Kong army's momentum became even stronger, and Malaya was temporarily trapped in a hard battle. The five Hong Kong forwards frequently attacked the goal, but none of them hit the target. At 35 minutes, the Malay army won a corner kick. The landing point was excellent. The center forward caught up and kicked the ball over the net, which was a pity. Before long, the three Malay forwards charged straight to the goal. The ball landed and advanced quickly like an arrow. The steel gate saved the ball by lying down and catching it, which was a wonderful posture. Guan Xinde was also injured and fell to the ground. He was carried out of the stadium for treatment by the Boy Scouts. Afterwards, the Malay army surrounded and attacked the Hong Kong goal five times, but all of them were defused by the Bao steel gate. When it was about to end, the Malay army won another opportunity for a corner kick, again and again. Just as he was about to raise his foot, the competition time had arrived. The Hong Kong army won the right to the final with a score of 3-2.

Guangdong replaced Tan Jiangbai with a defensive player due to Mai's injury and continued to fight. The cannons blazed, and the fighters of Bianfang team were furious. In the second half, the Guangdong side changed its strategy, mobilized its military strength, and the momentum was extremely strong. A General Review of the Skills of the Four Teams – Hong Kong is the Most Lively, but Its Inner Defense is Inferior – Malaya is Good at Passing, but Lacks Power in Shooting – Shanghai is Slow and Good at Defense – Guangdong is Extremely Fortunate and Overly Impulsive 224

In summary, the battles of the Hong Kong, Malaya, Guangdong, and Shanghai football teams yesterday showed that their strengths were comparable. The Hong Kong five forwards were the most lively and rapid. The left and right wings, Cao Guicheng and Zheng Jiliang, both had the skills of flying legs. The ball king Li Huitang responded to the left and right, dribbled past the defense line, and his arrows never missed the target. This is the way to win. However, the inner defense line seemed a bit weak. Fortunately, there was the Bao steel gate to guard the final checkpoint, so that the entire army had no worries. Otherwise, it would be difficult to obtain the final victory. The Malayan team's passing was magical, and its long and short passes and defense line were also well-matched. However, the five forwards lacked experience in shooting, and they often panicked and scattered at critical moments, or shot without hitting the target, which was a major problem. The Shanghai five forwards were slow, especially the two wings. Sun Jinshun and Li Taichen were both fat and could not run flexibly, which was a disadvantage. The defense line was the best in Shanghai. The goalkeeper Zhang Rongcai's qualifications were shallow, but in yesterday's battle, he can be said to have fulfilled his duty. The Guangdong team was brave and good at fighting. The five forwards' desperate efforts were admirable. The feet of Tan Jiangbai and Xu Yahui can be called unparalleled at the time. However, sometimes the whole army was overly impulsive and lacked cultivation. When winning, they were good at advancing and retreating, but when they failed, it was difficult to control them. Before reaching the stage of perfection, they should add some cultivation.
