Men's Baseball Shanghai Wins Baseball Championship, Liang Fuchu and Gan Zhen's Great Contributions, Seven to Two Victory Over Previous Champion Guangdong 225

In this year's baseball championship, Shanghai seized it from Guangdong, Guangdong was second, Beiping was third, Hebei was fourth, and the baseball battle of heroes vying for supremacy has now come to an end.

Great Hero Glorifies Shanghai's History

Baseball games at the National Games started in the second session, with North China winning the first championship, East China in the third, Hong Kong in the fourth, Guangdong in the fifth, and Shanghai in this session. Shanghai played a total of three games, first defeating Hunan, then Hebei, and finally defeating Guangdong to win the championship. Among the three games, the most important and exciting was the game against Guangdong. At that time, both sides were evenly matched, and the outcome was still unknown. In the fourth inning, veteran Liang Fuchu, based on his 38 years of rich experience, hit an unexpected sacrifice hit, first opening the scoring for the Shanghai team. In addition, pitcher Gan Zhen's ball was twisting and powerful, and the athletes of South China were all subdued by his ball, and even a small advance was difficult. Therefore, there were few enemy traces within Shanghai's defense, and his contribution to protecting the territory and securing the people was great. This person has glorified the historical record, and at the same time, all the team members have also done their duty, dominating the country, which is a matter of fact.

Former Champion Comes with a Preemptive Strike

The Guangdong team, the former champion, had talented people, excellent base-stealing skills, and hitting techniques. It was a pity that pitcher Yu Bohui could not exert his consistent powerful arm strength and exposed his weaknesses greatly in the seventh inning, opening the door to the enemy, almost unable to leave the field. In the first inning, the Guangdong team took the lead in attacking, worth four balls, walked to first base, and took advantage of the unpreparedness to steal second base again, which was a clear sign of an unfavorable start. But Lin stole to third base again, and Yu Bohui was retired after three hits. Gao Hanen came up to bat and came with a preemptive strike, hitting a single that went past first base. Lin knew that the opportunity could not be missed, and quickly returned, making the first contribution for Guangdong. Zhou Zhaojun was caught at first base, and Guangdong turned from offense to defense, waiting for Shanghai to attack. Shanghai was repeatedly disadvantaged. At the end of the first inning, Guangdong had one point, and Shanghai had zero. In the second and third innings, both sides were under strict surveillance, and they were bound by strategies. Although Shanghai's He Qionghua got a double in the second inning, and Liang ChengSong got a single in the second inning, they were unable to fulfill their ambitions due to their weak forces.

The Heroes Make a Big Scene in the Fourth Inning

In the fourth inning, Guangdong's first attack was unfavorable. When it was Shanghai's turn, hits came one after another. Zeng Ruikang hit and reached base, and Gan Cheng also hit a single, Zeng reached third base, and Gan stayed at first base. Veteran Liang Fuchu had a flash of inspiration and took advantage of the unpreparedness, lightly touching the ball to make a sacrifice hit, and Zeng returned to score, opening the scoring on the scorebook. Gan advanced to second base, and Liang reached first base. He Qionghua hit another single, and Gan and Liang each advanced one base, all bases were full. He Xiancheng came on the field, the pitcher gave in, and each advanced one base, and Gan slowly returned to base. When An Lesheng attacked, Liang also took advantage of the fielding error and ran to fourth base. At that time, Shanghai had scored three consecutive points. Continuing to return were He Xiancheng, An Lesheng, Zhou Jun, and Liang ChengSong, who won a total of seven points, while Guangdong got nothing. In the fifth inning, neither side scored. In the sixth inning, Guangdong's Gao Hanen hit and reached base, stole a base, was injured, and was replaced by Liu Duming. Huang Youxun hit a single, and Liu replaced Gao to return to base. Huang Zhaoxiong also hit a single, but Huang Youxun was caught before returning to base. All the efforts were abandoned. In the following innings, the pitchers of both sides showed their skills, and the attackers changed hands. In the second half of the ninth inning, Shanghai, with the victory in hand, decided to give up. As a result, Shanghai won seven to two. Men's and Women's National Arts: Shuttlecock Kicking Spectacular 239

The morning of the 18th featured a shuttlecock (Jiao Ti) kicking performance as part of the national arts program. The afternoon showcased the finals of the paired weapons competition. Archery judge Yang Jiaren also participated in the shuttlecock kicking performance. Furthermore, judges Zhang Weizhong and Yang Jiaren demonstrated archery skills, displaying both technical precision and a variety of techniques. Details are as follows:

Beijing Wins First

The shuttlecock kicking event commenced at the gymnasium on the morning of the 18th. Only seven participants took part in the Jiao Ti performance, with one withdrawing. Beijing's Dai Jinyao showcased excellent posture and a high number of kicks, reaching 140. Shanghai competitors secured the second, third, and fourth positions. Zhejiang's competitor earned fifth place. Beijing's Tang Rangmin, achieved only one kick on the first attempt before the shuttlecock touched the ground, and only four kicks on the second attempt. Due to the poor results, he was not selected.

Ranking No. of Clicks Name Unit Score

1 1818 Dai Jinyao Beijing 140 kicks

2 1855 Cao Hanjie Shanghai

3 1856 Chen Changfu Shanghai

4 1857 Chen Hongtai Shanghai

5 1774 Xie Shu'an Zhejiang

Spectacular Performance

Archery judge Yang Jiaren also participated in the shuttlecock kicking performance. Mr. Yang displayed great energy and agile movements. He prepared nine shuttlecocks with red, white, blue, and yellow feathers. He began by standing on a bench, kicking in the Jianzi style, then descended to perform on the ground. The first technique was "Three Rings Encircling the Moon" (kicking the shuttlecock upwards with the right foot, forming a circle with both hands, allowing the shuttlecock to fall through the circle, then kicking it upwards again). The second was "Buddha's Crown Jewel" (kicking the shuttlecock from the right toe onto the head, then back down to the right toe). The third was "On-the-Spot Pulling Up Onions" and "Mountain Immortal Entering the Cave" (placing a copper plate on the head, arranging shuttlecocks on the ground, lifting each shuttlecock upwards with the heel of the right foot, catching it on the toe, and guiding the shuttlecock into the plate on the head). The fourth was "Kicking Towards the Sky" (kicking upwards with the right foot, then catching the shuttlecock with the sole of the right foot). The fifth was "Five Branches Concentrating in the Heart" (kicking five shuttlecocks into the copper plate on the head), which was the most spectacular. Other impressive techniques included "Embracing the Moon in the Arms," "Falling Moon Golden Rooster," "Falling Frame Piece Horse Jumping Fish in the Air," "White Snake Spitting Out Its Tongue," and "Double Phoenix Piercing the Ears," all demonstrating remarkable kicking skills. Upon completion of the performance, the audience universally regarded it as a spectacle and praised it endlessly.

Rescheduled Finals

Furthermore, the second and third place winners from the weightlifting middleweight finals from the previous day, as well as the sixth-place winner from the paired martial arts finals, performed again yesterday morning and afternoon due to tied scores. As a result, the second place winner for the weightlifting middleweight division was Lu Li Shengzhang, and the third place winner was Weng Kangting. Additionally, the sixth-place winner for the men's martial arts paired finals performed yesterday. The decision was made in favor of Yu Cheng Shende against Zheng Shouxin.

Women's 400-Meter Relay Issue Resolved; Beijing Team Also Disqualified; Qualification of Beijing Athlete Yang Chunfu Under Investigation; Two Improvements to Be Implemented for Future Relay Finals 242

Regarding the issue of the women's 400-meter relay, both the Beijing and Shanghai teams ran out of their lanes. Following Shanghai's protest, the judging committee convened to discuss the matter. The third meeting was held at the general affairs office of the sports field yesterday morning at 10:30 AM. Attending were the committee chairman Zhang Boling, members Wang Zhengting, Shen Siliang, Song Ruhai, Qiu Jixiang, Hao Gengsheng, Zhang Huilan, Chen Kun, Chen Kui Sheng, Chu Minyi, Dong Shouyi, Chen Menghai, and the general leader of the Beijing team, Li Zhou, who was invited to attend for consultation.

Differing Opinions

After the meeting commenced, the chairman first read out the key points of Shanghai's protest: (1) The Shanghai team was disqualified from the women's 400-meter relay due to running out of their lane. However, the Beijing team, which also ran out of their lane, has not been officially disqualified, which seems unfair. (2) In the all-around athletics 400-meter relay race, Nanjing athlete Yang Chunfu participated in the Jiangsu first district preliminary round. Please investigate and disqualify him. A discussion then began. Regarding the first point, some committee members believed that the photo evidence from Wang Kai proved that the Beijing team did run out of their lane. However, because a Shanghai team member encroached on their lane, the Beijing team members were forced to run into another lane, so their mistake was understandable. Other committee members argued that the Beijing team members should have reported the Shanghai team's encroachment on their lane to the inspectors on the spot during the race and requested a re-run. They should not have also run into another lane. Now that they have also violated the rules, they should of course be disqualified according to the regulations.

Decision to Disqualify

After much discussion, it was decided to disqualify the Beijing team. Regarding the second point, it was generally agreed that if Nanjing athlete Yang Chunfu participated in the preliminary rounds for two units, his qualification to participate in the games should be cancelled. According to the joint notice from the competition and judging committees to the general leaders of each unit, they should self-report any issues with their athletes' qualifications. If they do not self-report and are discovered, the entire team will be disqualified, even if only one person is unqualified. Therefore, the qualification of the entire 400-meter relay team should be cancelled. However, there is no conclusive evidence at this time whether Yang Chunfu participated in the preliminary rounds for two units. A decision will be made based on the actual situation after investigation. The discussion concluded around 11:00 AM. The committee's resolution was as follows: "Since the Shanghai team was disqualified for running out of their lane, and the photo shows that the Beijing team also ran out of their lane, they should also be disqualified." The resolution was passed.

Two Lessons Learned

After the committee members Zhang Boling, Wang Zhengting, and others settled the case, they proposed two points based on the experience of this dispute to improve future rules: (1) When defining the lanes, the number of lanes used should correspond to the number of teams participating, with no empty lanes in between to avoid lane infringement. (2) The lane numbers should also be clearly marked at the turns. These proposals were unanimously approved. It was also heard that the committee has now settled the two protest issues raised by the Shanghai team and will reply to the team by letter. (Note that the women's 400-meter relay was originally sixth place. Due to the Shanghai team being disqualified, it rose to fifth place. Now that it has also been disqualified, only four teams have placed: first place to the Guangdong team, second place to the Malaya team, third place to the Qingdao team, and fourth place to the Fujian team. Fifth and sixth places are vacant.)

Issue of Hebei National Arts Athlete Bu Enfu; Beijing Withdraws Protest; Deposit Returned 243

It is reported that the Beijing general leader has withdrawn the protest regarding Hebei Province middleweight athlete Bu Enfu, as they did not want to cause further trouble. The judging committee has also returned the deposit.

Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission Invites Overseas Chinese Athletes to Beijing 245

(Nanjing, 18th) Chairman Chen of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission dispatched Chen Chunpu, the director of the Overseas Chinese Education Department of the Commission, to Shanghai on the 18th to invite the overseas Chinese athlete delegations from Malaya, Java, and the Philippines to visit Beijing after the games. The original letter stated: "You have traveled far and wide to return to the motherland, demonstrating your heartfelt patriotism. Your impressive achievements have added luster to the games. The Commission, responsible for overseas Chinese affairs, has always been concerned about the education of overseas Chinese youth. Promoting sports and strengthening physical fitness are essential for the revival of the nation. Your understanding of this is deeply gratifying. After the closing ceremony of the games, the Commission plans to invite you to visit Beijing to see the political and economic construction of the motherland in recent years, so that you can gain a deeper understanding. Please inform us of your departure date two days in advance so that we can prepare."

Philippine Basketball Team Prepares to Compete in Hankou; Expresses Regret That Film Omitted Them 246

The Philippine Chinese Overseas delegation traveled a long way to return to the country to participate in the National Games. The men's basketball team had considerable strength and fought through many matches before being eliminated by Nanjing in the semi-finals. However, their overall appearance was very good. The general leader of the team did not come this time. According to team captain Mr. Yang, the team is now committed to an engagement in Hankou and will prepare to perform there after the closing ceremony of the games. If this cannot be arranged, they plan to return to the Philippines on the 21st. He also stated that the team spent a long time preparing to return to the country for the games, with the sole purpose of connecting with compatriots in the country and dispelling any doubts that we have abandoned the motherland. Therefore, they traveled thousands of miles to come and observed many sporting events, which was very beneficial. However, in the film taken at this games, each province and city unit was included, and the movements and lives of athletes from Malaya were even more detailed, but the Philippine team was not included. Perhaps this was an oversight by the organizing committee, but if this film is shown to the overseas Chinese in the Philippines, it will create a negative impression of the team. Therefore, they feel great regret.

National Sports Association; National Congress of Delegates; Zhang Boling and Others Re-elected as Third Board of Directors 249

The Chinese National Sports Association held its National Congress of Delegates last night at 7:00 PM at the YMCA in Ba Xian Qiao. Attendees included President Zhang Boling, Vice President Wu Tiecheng (represented by Shen Siliang), Directors Chu Minyi, Ma Yuehan, Yuan Dunli, Hao Gengsheng, Gao Zi, Jin Zencheng, Cao Yunxiang, Chief Secretary Shen Siliang, Secretary Zhou Jiaqi, Song Ruhai from the Wuhan Sports Association, and delegates from various regions, including Gu Yuqi (Henan), Yang Xiaozhai (Guizhou), Zhang Deshan (Qinghai), Wu Chunwu (Yunnan), Zhao Wenzao (Hebei), Liu Shen [character missing] (Sichuan), Wu Demao (Fujian), Shao Rugan (Shanghai), Zhou Ruhai (Xikang), Zang Qifang (Liaoning), Zhou Guoliang (Rehe), Hu Anshan (Jilin), Liang Zhi (Nanjing), Luo Liangzhu (Anhui), Zhang Yong (Shanxi), Shang Shangmei (Shandong), Wang Zhuoran (Harbin), Zhu Jiasheng (Zhejiang), Zhang Jiwu (Tianjin), Song Junfu (Qingdao), Zhang Ziyao (Shaanxi), Xu Minhui (Guangdong), Chen Shi (Hubei), Li Zhou (Beiping), Wu Bangwei (Jiangsu), Wu Yunlong (Jiangxi), Fang Kegang (Xiangnan), Yan Chengkun (Hong Kong), Lu Qihua (Guangxi), and others. The congress began with an opening speech by Chairman Zhang Boling, followed by a report on the work of the past two years by Chief Secretary Shen Siliang. The congress then discussed the constitution, and the representatives voted on the amendments, which were submitted to the Constitution Amendment Committee. The discussion concluded at 11:00 PM. The new board of directors was elected, and the list of those elected is as follows: Zhang Boling, Wang Zhengting, Hao Gengsheng, Chu Minyi, Wu Yunrui, Ma Yuehan, Shen Siliang, Yuan Dunli, Gao Zi, Zhu Jiahua, Dong Shouyi, Wu Tiecheng, Wang Zhuoran, Zhang Jiwu, and Song Junfu. The third board of directors will hold its first meeting at the New Asia Hotel on Sichuan Road this afternoon at 7:00 PM.

Location for Next North China Games Tentatively Set at Two Places: Beiping or Xi'an; Executive Committee of North China Sports Federation Held Discussion Yesterday 250

Taking advantage of the National Games, the executive committee members of the North China Sports Federation gathered in Shanghai and held a discussion yesterday at the YMCA in Ba Xian Qiao. Over a dozen members attended to discuss the location for the next North China Games. After a long discussion, the issue remained unresolved. The location is tentatively set at either Beiping or Xi'an in Shaanxi. If neither of these locations can host the games, Qingdao will be considered again.

Notable Events at National Games: Wrestling and Archery Champions Marry; Ma Wenkui and Ma Ruilan 251

At the [number missing] National Games, Ma Wenkui, the wrestling champion from Nanjing, and Ma Ruilan, the archery runner-up from Henan, were introduced by Hai Lanfen, the long-distance archery champion, and Ding Quanfu, the strength contest champion. They held their wedding ceremony at 3:00 PM yesterday at the Islamic Mosque at No. 70 Zhejiang Road. Qian Zhai Shan and Yang Songshan served as the hosts, while Ma Renfu, the father of the bride and a religious leader, and martial arts figures Wu Ziping, Tong Zhongyi, and Liu Buxian served as the witnesses. At 1:30 PM, Ah Heng Hadcheng, according to Islamic doctrine, read the Kabin (transliteration), witnessed the marriage, instructed them on religious doctrines, and gave a speech, while Liu Buxian also spoke, offering words of encouragement. The ceremony ended around 4:00 PM. The new couple, the Ma family, will return to Beijing on the 21st, and Mr. Ma Renfu will also leave Shanghai and return to Henan at the same time.

Education News

Shanghai Boy Scout Instructor Certification Exam Not Allowed 258

(Nanjing, 18th) The Shanghai Boy Scout Council held a Boy Scout Instructor Certification Exam. The Boy Scout General Association stated that any organization holding a certification must first draft certification rules and submit them to the association for approval before holding the exam. It has issued an order to stop the exam.

Measures for Private Chinese Schools in the Public Concession to Apply for Subsidies 259

During a recent meeting, the Municipal Council's Education Committee discussed the issue of subsidies for private Chinese schools. Prior to the meeting, the Municipal Council's Health Department submitted a report on the sanitation facilities of various private schools. The report stated that the sanitation facilities of 180 schools were up to standard and should be given subsidies. The date for issuing the subsidies is scheduled for around the second Friday after the end of each [quarter]. After these measures were approved by the Education Committee, all schools that have paid the Municipal Council's universal housing tax, have sanitary facilities up to standard, or are temporarily considered to be up to standard, can apply for subsidies. The Education Committee also drafted the following four measures to be submitted to the Board of Directors for approval: (1) In addition to the third-quarter subsidies for this year, the subsidies for the three schools that were previously rated as substandard should be temporarily suspended. Now that they have improved in accordance with the regulations of the Health Department, they should be paid retroactively. (2) The subsidies for the five substandard schools and the schools that are in arrears with the Municipal Council's universal housing tax should be temporarily suspended. (3) In accordance with the regulations, starting from the time when the subsidies should be obtained, the subsidies will no longer be issued to those who fail to improve their facilities in accordance with the regulations of the Health Department within six months. (4) Currently, one Chinese school is not located within the Public Concession, and its autumn subsidy will not be issued for the time being. It will be deferred to the next meeting, when the director of the Education Department will submit a detailed report for further review. All of the above proposed measures have been approved by the Municipal Council's Board of Directors at its recent regular meeting.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

What Modern Chinese Women Need is a New Morality 260

— Xing An

Jinan Correspondence: Mrs. Han, wife of the Provincial Governor of Shandong, and others, having recently observed that modern Chinese women either vainly pursue frivolousness and lack self-discipline, abandoning their inherent responsibilities, or are weak, incompetent, and ignorant, stubbornly adhering to outdated customs, resulting in the near-total burying of the old Zhou dynasty morality, the obliteration of the true spirit of women, the more developed women's rights become, the more decadent life becomes, the more advanced civilization becomes, the more corrupt customs become. If this situation is not urgently rectified, advocating for women's rights will only serve to undermine them, and the world's ingrained concept of valuing men over women will never be eliminated. In order to correct these bad habits of women and revive women's morality, a special alliance has been formed with enlightened women from all walks of life to establish the Shandong Women's Morality Promotion Association, with the aim of improving women's lives.

"Modern Chinese women, those who embrace modernity, vainly pursue frivolousness and lack self-discipline, abandoning their inherent responsibilities," this is the truth. "Those who adhere to tradition are weak, incompetent, and ignorant, stubbornly adhering to outdated customs," this is also the truth. But why is this the case? To put it bluntly: this is caused by the old Chinese morality! Because Chinese women have always lived under the shackles of old morality, without any freedom. Therefore, those who embrace modernity, once exposed to new ideas, must be unrestrained and domineering. Those who adhere to tradition, being ignorant and uneducated, can only stubbornly adhere to outdated customs. Therefore, the way to remedy this is to fundamentally overthrow the old morality and rebuild a new morality for women to follow. This is the only solution. Otherwise, the lives of Chinese women will probably never have any hope of improvement! However, the Shandong Women's Morality Promotion Association is lamenting the burying of inherent morality and wants to use the means of restoring women's morality to improve women's lives. This is a mistake.

Speaking of the issue of women's rights, this is what modern Chinese women must strive for. Because Chinese women's rights have long been deprived of them! However, the Shandong Women's Morality Promotion Association says, "The more developed women's rights become, the more decadent life becomes, the more advanced civilization becomes, the more corrupt customs become." Originally, in present-day China, women do not even have women's rights to speak of, let alone development? Even if Chinese women's rights have made considerable progress, this should not lead to the decadence of women's lives. The lives of modern Chinese women are indeed decadent in some aspects. However, this is definitely not the fault of the development of women's rights, but rather another factor that leads to this decadence. Moreover, this is only the case for a small number of Chinese women. Is it really that women's rights are undesirable? The Shandong Women's Morality Promotion Association believes that "If this situation is not urgently rectified, advocating for women's rights will only serve to undermine them, and some people's concept of valuing men over women will never be eliminated." Then, may I ask, will restoring women's morality guarantee women's rights and eliminate the concept of valuing men over women? The reason why Chinese women today do not have women's rights and why the world values men over women is all due to the influence of the old morality!

In short, the organization of the Shandong Women's Morality Promotion Association is either intentionally regressive or taking the wrong path. Let us reiterate here. In the future, if we want to improve the lives of Chinese women, it lies not in restoring the old morality, but in establishing a new morality!

Flower House 261

— Xiong

In the courtyard of the new residence, a row of parasol trees is planted along the steps. They stand tall with their upright, thick trunks, higher than the roof of the building. In summer, their lush, dense leaves spread out like umbrellas, seemingly covering the top of the building, blocking the scorching sunlight and bringing gentle breezes. When the leaves sway, they create beautiful patterns on the windows, making one feel that the summer sun also has its charm.

The host of the residence is an elder of about fifty years old. He lives here alone in solitude, accompanied by a child who enjoys catching cicadas and butterflies. I met him for the first time through a friend's introduction. He said he was very happy to have a cohabitant like me, as he felt too lonely. He gave me the impression of a recluse who had suffered a great shock.

The old man loves flowers as if they were his life, and there are hundreds of flowerpots arranged in the courtyard. The child is very experienced in planting flowers, and every morning he helps the host to divide branches, cultivate soil, water plants, and catch insects, acting with a care unlike his usual lively and playful self. Later, I learned that he was the son of the gardener who had previously been employed by the host.

Because of his love for flowers, the host specially used the strength of the parasol tree's trunk and branches to build a pergola that could cover the entire courtyard, covered with reed mats, which could be rolled up like a curtain. Naturally, this was also the child's responsibility.

Page 22

The host cares very much for the child. In ordinary conversations, he often acts like a little master. He often laments not having the money to build an exquisite flower house, saying, "That child is too hardworking. He serves these flowers without ever making a mistake!"

When I am idle, I lean against the window and watch the two of them touching and feeling in the courtyard, meticulously inspecting each pot. When they discover a diseased flower, they discuss it, considering how to treat and nurse it, often unable to make a decision for a long time. Then the host raises his head and speaks to me:

"Planting flowers is very interesting, but I hate those insects. There's simply no way to deal with them. You can't catch them all, and watching them die is like watching my own son die..."

He always shakes his head at the end, saying, "If only I could build a flower house!"

Then he strolls up to my room and pulls me to "play a game of chess." The host's chess skills are not very good. He loses to me nine times out of ten. And at this time, he loses even faster. After only a few moves, he pushes the chessboard away, saying, "I lost again," and strolls back to the courtyard.

The child, however, is capable. He sits on the steps, holding his head in his hands. He tries to search for planting experience from a corner of his little brain, or perhaps a story that his father told him that could revive the diseased flower. He sits there for a long time, unwilling to leave. Even if the host urges him, he will come up with various methods to rekindle the host's interest, and the two of them will go back to treating them.

This kind of situation happens often, and each time the child manages to revive the diseased flower.

After living here for a long time, the child and I became very close. One day, while we were fishing by the pond, I asked him about his planting experience, which led him to tell me the host's story:

The child has lived in the host's home since he was little. The host used to be an official and had a vast fortune. His old wife passed away early, and he had an only son, who squandered the host's wealth and was imprisoned for theft. So the host retreated to this only residence on the outskirts. He originally hired a gardener to decorate the garden of his mansion, priding himself on collecting and planting rare flowers in his garden to show off his wealth. Now he uses planting flowers to pass the lonely rest of his life. If a flower that is not worth a penny dies, he will scold his son all day long, to the point of neglecting food and sleep and becoming ill. "So," the child said, "when a diseased flower is discovered, I always try my best to save it. The host loves me dearly, and I can't bear to see him in his manic state."

I am glad that the host has such a loyal servant, but when I hear him say "If only I could build a flower house," I don't know what to say.

Passing Skirt Belt Mountain at Night 262

— Shen Wu

The sun has shrunk its head below the mountainside, and a burst of rosy glow reflects half of the mountains. The trails in the mountain depressions are gradually becoming sparse, and the gurgling sound of running water is still clearly reaching the ears. The pine forests and wild thorns appear particularly vibrant in the sunset glow. The mountain pits are as deep as bottomless pools. Everyone no longer dares to admire the scenery near or far, but focuses on carefully steadying their steps, fearing that a misstep will send them rolling into the mountain pit. At the same time, they are also fearful of the steep Skirt Belt Mountain ahead, where the mountain rats (a euphemism for bandits) are known for their ruthless methods, chilling the hearts of all who hear of them.

"Brother Zhuang, we who make a living this way are truly risking our lives. I'm really worried about Little Gouzi. He doesn't have a father, and his mother is truly suffering. You must take care of him on the road. He's young and doesn't know the dangers, and he'll rush ahead... If—alas, Uncle Huang said that those mountain rats won't let anyone off easily. They're afraid that a boss might be disguised as a porter. How could a group like ours not have someone with something of value?... Really, the mention of embroidered knives (a type of killing) is terrifying!... It's truly a 'nine deaths and one life.' I'm afraid not even one in ten can return safely!..." As I walked here, I couldn't help but recall Little Gouzi's mother's nagging requests every time we set off. The surrounding mountains are so towering and steep, and the road is so narrow. At every turn, or in the chaotic piles of long grass, those mountain rats could be lurking at any time. If we don't run into them, it will be our good luck. In the past, someone tried to set fire to the wild grass in the mountains, hoping to deprive the mountain rats of hiding places, but instead they were captured by the mountain rats and forced to undergo embroidered knives. How pitiful! To make a living on this road that treads the line between life and death!

"Little Gouzi! Pick up the pace, why are you dragging along like a sheep pulling an old ox? Aren't you afraid of falling behind in battle?"

As we slowly climbed up the dangerous road on Skirt Belt Mountain, Little Gouzi gradually slowed down. Old Song yelled at him casually. I turned back to take a quick glance. He really did look like an ant, struggling to walk, his timid eyes looking forward and then back. I couldn't help but urge him, "Little Gouzi, cheer up and hurry along. No one is going to wait for you!"

This young man, Little Gouzi, is not as his mother described him: someone who is unaware of the dangers. In our group, he is the youngest, but also the most timid. He always lags behind, and he never moves to the front unless his companions urge him repeatedly. He really doesn't seem like a young man!...

As we walked on the narrow road of the skirt belt, the sun had already set behind the mountain and was dozing off. The moon had not yet risen, and the surroundings were already a deep, dark sea of night. A few stars were trying hard to widen their eyes, but the mountain path was still shrouded in darkness. The chirping of insects, which had begun to fill the mountains and fields after sunset, now reached our ears even more clearly. Occasionally, there were also some "whoosh, whoosh" sounds as the mountain wind scoured through the trees. The sound was desolate and monotonous. Old Bamboo Head often said that this was a sign of tigers or mountain rats coming, but in reality, nothing ever happened afterwards. Sometimes, it was probably the cries of mountain birds, which made Old Bamboo Head suspect it was the crying of ghosts: "Unjustly wronged, I will know. I will burn paper money for you when I get back tonight, don't cry, let us walk well!... We have heard him murmuring and chanting like this more than once. Song Sen always deliberately joked with him: "Old Uncle Bamboo, she doesn't want your paper money, she wants you to be her companion. It's a female ghost!" Or, "He's not married yet. Bring your daughter tomorrow. We'll make her the Land Goddess of Skirt Belt Mountain!"

But as soon as Song Sen said this, Old Bamboo Head would shake his gray head and scold, "You'll be beheaded, there'll be retribution, how can you talk such nonsense? Toilet paper to wipe your mouth!"

But after Song Sen made a joke, everyone laughed heartily, and their hearts lightened. The Skirt Belt Mountain pass became much easier to cross.

The night was silent. In the bright moonlight, we slowly climbed from the top of the mountain to the bottom of the depression, crossing one mountain after another. We ourselves seemed like ghosts, forgetting that we still had a life.

Jiangnan 263

— Luo Zhihua

—One of the Scattered Southern Travels—

Before I came to Jiangnan, my heart longed for Jiangnan as one longs for the wilderness; when I saw the wilderness, I longed for the wilderness of Jiangnan as one longs for Jiangnan.

The people in the third-class carriage were either quietly flipping through magazines or their favorite novels, or discussing current events with those sitting next to them. Still others were discussing the beauty of women.

My surroundings were empty, not even a single person. Their conversations rarely affected my thoughts. So I had plenty of leisure to think about some questions. Most of these questions arose from other people's conversations. My head was close to the window, watching the undulating land outside, and my tired heart was quieted by the sound of the train wheels.

When I was in school, I heard a teacher say that Jiangnan is beautiful. He was an aesthetic poet, and he said that in Nanjing, if you go to Ming Xiaoling Mausoleum and Taicheng, and look around, almost all you see is lush greenery. He even recited his poetry:

Whose family's oil sea has burst its banks,

The wilderness of Jiangnan is all green and oily.

A girl in green goes in without a trace,

A branch of red peach blooms, dreamlike and free!

Therefore, I dreamed that the wilderness of Jiangnan was a vast sea of green, with soft, grassy meadows spreading out across the vast plains, as vibrant and luminous as flowing velvet. The mountains and soil were also like this, looking like waterfalls about to flow down, the whole mountain being a huge piece of glass.

So, I thought of this scene. My head rested on the window, watching the endless road recede into the distance.

At this moment, a gentlemanly man moved over and sat opposite me. He looked at my simple clothes and luggage and said in a slightly disdainful tone:

—Oh, where are you going? (The pure

Page 23

Beijing dialect is pleasant to hear, but his manner was really unbearable: his head waggling as he asked me.)

—Me? Going to Shanghai!

—Where are you from?

Beijing!

—Oh, Beijing! (He paused) Beijing is a good place!

Then his attitude changed, perhaps because he realized that I could also speak Beijing dialect.

—Beijing, ah, it really is a good place. I'm also from there, going to Shanghai... Have you been to Shanghai?... No? That place is really annoying. The most annoying thing is the toilets! Look at Beijing, it's so comfortable to live in. Not to mention anything else, places like Beihai Park, Zhongnanhai, and Shichahai are all fun. In Shanghai, staying one more day is like losing ten years of life!... Alas, it's so dirty!

As he spoke, it seemed as if everything in front of him and around him was dirty. He wiped his nose with a silk handkerchief and said a lot more. What he emphasized most was that "it doesn't matter for rich people," as if to say, "A poor wretch like you has to smell the toilet smell!" In order to maintain my own solemn attitude, I simply replied to him a couple of times, and then he ran off to another place. I heard him still talking about things in Beijing.

His words did not make me disgusted with Jiangnan: I still loved Jiangnan. The reason was that I hated the gray North Country, the weather that was filled with gray sand all day long, and the severe cold and scorching heat. But Jiangnan had not yet arrived. Perhaps Jiangnan was still far away.

But I finally got to see the wilderness of Jiangnan.

First, when we were about to arrive in Pukou, I was very skeptical about where these fields were: all of them were bare red earth. Not a single blade of green grass. At that time, I thought: this is Jiangbei, let's go past Nanjing and see again, maybe it will be better.

After passing Nanjing, the scenes of drought changed one after another. Some were endless stretches of red. Although some places had grass, it was dry, yellow grass. After passing several rivers, they were all dry, peeling, and lying there.

Where was the green grassland, the lovely Jiangnan!

Drought and water diverted had covered up this green grassland.

The poet's deceptive words had strengthened my hopeful belief, and the iron reality shattered this dream of longing. My heart was carried by the train to another place.

Song Introduction 265

To the Nightingale

Nightingale, your song is so graceful and light; Nightingale, your song is so clear and moving; Ah! Poets are intoxicated by you, Ah! Lovers embrace in carefree joy! But please bow your head and look at these sinners in hell, in deep darkness and pain! Unwarm clothes, Unfilled stomachs, Who knows about the misery of their lives? Who knows? Nightingale! Please, for them, send out some roars of forced resistance, Encourage those despondent and suicidal, wandering on the wrong path; Cut through thorns and briars, and move forward hand in hand! Nightingale, your song must be tragic and powerful, a summons, invigorating! Nightingale, your song must be so solemn and moving! Ah—please don't just praise the gurgling spring in the secluded valley: Please don't, just sing the bright moon in the sky!

Radio Waves 266

Miss Jiang Lingdi, an amateur piano virtuoso, hasn't even been on the radio yet, but yesterday the newspapers were already praising her, even writing about her age, origin, and temperament. The only things missing are Miss Jiang's zodiac sign, birth time, address, number of lovers, number of umbrella hooks, and number of supporters. In your spare time, please, Mr. Great Reporter who wrote this news yesterday, add these details to broaden our horizons and have a laugh!

The Xinmin News Agency wrote a piece titled "Yan Fei, Ye Ying, and Ye Hong Go to Taiwan...Incorrect." Meng Ying wrote a piece titled "Fat Sister Goes to Taiwan with Yan Fei, Ye Ying, and Ye Hong." The former and latter pieces were published on the same day yesterday, which is quite confusing. I don't know which piece is true? However, as far as I know, the Xinmin News Agency is writing nonsense without basis, while Meng Ying plagiarized the "Radio Waves" of the 4th, only reversing the order. Do the two of you think that's right? Does the editor think I'm wrong? (Silver Rain) The editor was inattentive, so both news items were published. It's hard to tell which is true or false for the time being. In the future, I hope readers will point out errors when they find them, but "tofu" is rejected (Editor).

The matter of eating tofu can be found everywhere. Movies

Introduction to "The Moon Bends" 267

The season has reached late autumn, and the October wind brings a sad autumn mood to those who are disappointed. On bright moonlit nights, we may hear this folk song, faintly transmitted from the mouth of a resentful woman in the deep Min region.

The moon bends, shining on the nine continents, some families are happy, some families are worried!

Some couples share the same bed, some are wandering outside.

This is a popular and well-known folk poem, depicting the men and women of the world, who are forced to travel and are oppressed by the environment, causing them to drift east and fear the west, each drinking the bitter wine of separation. On the same night of reunion, some couples follow each other, enjoying human bliss to the fullest, while others think of their hometowns while gazing at the moon and miss their loved ones in the wind, which is extremely miserable. "The Moon Bends" is a five-act drama that Mr. Xu Zhuodai adapted based on the folk song as the main thread, weaving the joys and sorrows of life into a touching and poignant story.

"The Moon Bends" is led by Ms. Hu Die, with the entire cast of male and female actors from the Mingxing Company participating. After more than two months of rehearsal, it is completely proficient. It will be released at the Xinguang Grand Theater in the near future. This is the unprecedented large-scale drama movement of the Mingxing Company, and this once-in-a-lifetime grand event is of course the most sensational event recently.

The outline of the plot of "The Moon Bends" is as follows:

The opening of the prologue of "The Moon Bends" is set in a certain city four or five years ago, on the night of the Mid-Autumn Festival. In a happy family, a young couple is entertaining guests and enjoying themselves under the moon, but a flash flood suddenly erupts, and this gathering is immediately filled with an atmosphere of terror.

Because of the flash flood, a huge flood was brewed, and for a time, cries of mourning were heard everywhere, and refugees were on the road. The people were all in a panic, like stray dogs. Among them, the young couple, Tao Zifang and his wife Manzhu, and their daughter Xue'er, were also separated, and their whereabouts were unknown to each other.

After Manzhu was separated from her husband by the flood, she had to take her daughter and live through miserable years under difficult living conditions. Manzhu, because she missed her husband and the vows between husband and wife, had been living her miserable and impoverished life for four or five years. She has experienced vicissitudes of life, but she always foolishly hopes that her husband will return safely. Many people advised her to remarry, but she refused. Jin Huanzhang, a childhood classmate who helped her the most, loved her deeply, but she also politely refused him. However, that man also rejected the love of many women for her. She only has one unwavering wish: that her husband can return gracefully and relive the sweet years.

This is the last scene: Cao Zhu has experienced hardship and finally met her husband by chance while working as a servant. However, everything has changed. Zifang has become the husband of a noble lady. When they met, he was like a stranger, pretending not to recognize her, and unintentionally, he killed Manzhu's, and also his own daughter Xue'er. Manzhu was extremely sad, but at the same time, she woke up from a dream, knowing that a woman's reliance on her husband is just a dream, because men are often unreliable. Although the tragedy was revealed on the spot, the noble lady blamed Zifang for a while, and because of sympathy, she was willing to let her live together. But in the end, she resolutely left her husband. The tragedy of life on the stage ended in a tragic atmosphere.

"The Moon Bends" has such a touching plot, rich in dramatic life performances, joys and sorrows, and touching poignancy, which naturally can stir the emotions of the audience everywhere. In addition, the great scenery on the stage, such as flash floods, floods, etc., is probably an unprecedented initiative on the stage of our country?

The actors of "The Moon Bends" are: Ms. Hu Die plays Manzhu, Wang Xianzai plays Tao Zifang, who abandons the old and embraces the new and indulges in pleasure, Gao Zhanfei plays Manzhu's childhood classmate Jin Huanzhang, Gu Lanjun plays Huanzhang's cousin, who writes "love" as "change", Yan Yuexian plays a socialite, Zhu Qiuhen plays the noble lady Yingyu, Shu Xiuwen plays Mother Chen, etc. All of them are the best talents in the film industry, so their every move, every frown and smile, are subtle and in harmony with the characters in the play. Their acting skills on the screen have long been widely praised, but this time, their large-scale performance on the stage of film actors has also reached the pinnacle of their superior stage artistic performance.

Readers who love drama, wait and see!
